Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<br>





tested os:ubuntu 22.04

tested chrome:



<span class="line"><!---->tested chrome:<!----></span>

<br>





Chromium 108.0.5312.0



<span class="line"><!---->Chromium 108.0.5312.0<!----></span>

<br>





This issue can be reproduced in scenarios where automation tools are used, such as puppeteer.



<span class="line"><!---->This issue can be reproduced in scenarios where automation tools are used, such as puppeteer.<!----></span>



<br>





1. install puppeteer.



<span class="line"><!---->1. install puppeteer.<!----></span>



<br>





2. node ./test.js



<span class="line"><!---->2. node ./test.js<!----></span>

3. immediately crash.

Author: Simon Zünd <



<span class="line"><!---->Author: Simon Zünd &lt;<!----></span>





szuend@chromium.org



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/szuend@chromium.org"><!---->szuend@chromium.org<!----></a>

Date: Fri Sep 30 11:47:11 2022



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Fri Sep 30 11:47:11 2022<!----></span>

<br>





[inspector] Fix user-after-free bug around async evaluations



<span class="line"><!---->[inspector] Fix user-after-free bug around async evaluations<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL fixes a use-after-free bug where we try to access an



<span class="line"><!---->This CL fixes a use-after-free bug where we try to access an<!----></span>



<br>





`InjectedScript` object after it died. This can happen when we



<span class="line"><!---->`InjectedScript` object after it died. This can happen when we<!----></span>



<br>





transition into JS and back and the context group dies in the mean



<span class="line"><!---->transition into JS and back and the context group dies in the mean<!----></span>



<br>





time (e.g. because of a navigation). Normally we check for this but



<span class="line"><!---->time (e.g. because of a navigation). Normally we check for this but<!----></span>



<br>





we missed a call to `Promise#then`.



<span class="line"><!---->we missed a call to `Promise#then`.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The access that triggers the UaF is when we try to stash away the



<span class="line"><!---->The access that triggers the UaF is when we try to stash away the<!----></span>



<br>





protocol callback function after returning from `Promise#then`.



<span class="line"><!---->protocol callback function after returning from `Promise#then`.<!----></span>



<br>





The callback function is responsible for sending the protocol



<span class="line"><!---->The callback function is responsible for sending the protocol<!----></span>



<br>





response back to DevTools containing the result of the evaluation.



<span class="line"><!---->response back to DevTools containing the result of the evaluation.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





There are two objects with different lifetimes involved:



<span class="line"><!---->There are two objects with different lifetimes involved:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  - InjectedScript: Owns the `EvaluationCallback`. We keep a



<span class="line"><!---->  - InjectedScript: Owns the `EvaluationCallback`. We keep a<!----></span>



<br>





    a reference in case the context group dies. This allows us to



<span class="line"><!---->    a reference in case the context group dies. This allows us to<!----></span>



<br>





    cancel any pending evaluate requests.



<span class="line"><!---->    cancel any pending evaluate requests.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  - ProtocolPromiseHandler: Has a reference to `EvaluationCallback`.



<span class="line"><!---->  - ProtocolPromiseHandler: Has a reference to `EvaluationCallback`.<!----></span>



<br>





    The handler itself is managed by the V8 GC via `v8::External`



<span class="line"><!---->    The handler itself is managed by the V8 GC via `v8::External`<!----></span>



<br>





    and a weak `v8::Global`.



<span class="line"><!---->    and a weak `v8::Global`.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When the `ProtocolPromiseHandler` wants use the callback to send



<span class="line"><!---->When the `ProtocolPromiseHandler` wants use the callback to send<!----></span>



<br>





a response, it needs to take ownership first.



<span class="line"><!---->a response, it needs to take ownership first.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We could invert the ownership but it's preferable for evaluation



<span class="line"><!---->We could invert the ownership but it's preferable for evaluation<!----></span>



<br>





callbacks to die together with execution contexts and not when the



<span class="line"><!---->callbacks to die together with execution contexts and not when the<!----></span>



<br>





GC feels like it.



<span class="line"><!---->GC feels like it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





We fix the UaF by using an `InjectedSript::ContextScope` and reloading



<span class="line"><!---->We fix the UaF by using an `InjectedSript::ContextScope` and reloading<!----></span>



<br>





the `InjectedScript` after we return from `Promise#then`. Then



<span class="line"><!---->the `InjectedScript` after we return from `Promise#then`. Then<!----></span>



<br>





we can take proper ownership of the callback and use it in case the



<span class="line"><!---->we can take proper ownership of the callback and use it in case the<!----></span>



<br>





call failed.



<span class="line"><!---->call failed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





R=



<span class="line"><!---->R=<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

           * there's spacing. */
